<P style="page-break-before:always; margin:0pt; line-height:14pt; font-
family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt" align=center><B>PART I</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:5pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Big 
Sky Energy Corporation (&#147;Big Sky&#148; or the &#147;Company&#148;) is 
filing this Amendment No. 2 to its Annual Report on Form 10-KSB/A for the year 
ended December 31, 2004 (this &#147;Amendment&#148;) to reflect the amendment 
and restatement of its Consolidated Financial Statements for the year ended 
December 31, 2004 to reflect adjustments determined to be necessary as a result 
of an internal investigation of the treatment of certain portions of an farm-out
agreement entered into by one of its subsidiaries. </P>
<P style="margin-top:5pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The 
Annual Report on Form 10-KSB for the year ended December 31, 2004 was initially 
filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission on April 15, 2005 and 
Amendment No. 1 thereto was filed on August 19, 2005. This Amendment No. 2 on 
Form 10-KSB/A is being filed to reflect restatements of the following financial 
statements: </P>
<P style="margin-top:4.15pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-
indent:-18pt; font-family:Wingdings">&#8226;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; padding-left:36pt; font-
family:Wingdings"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman">Consolidated balance sheet as at 
December 31, 2004; </FONT></P>
<P style="margin-top:4.15pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-
indent:-18pt; font-family:Wingdings">&#8226;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:4.15pt; padding-left:36pt; font-
family:Wingdings"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman">Consolidated statements of cash 
flows for the year ended December 31, 2004;</FONT></P>
<P style="margin-top:4.15pt; margin-bottom:-12pt; padding-left:36pt; text-
indent:-18pt; font-family:Wingdings">&#8226;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; padding-left:36pt; font-
family:Wingdings"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman">and to make certain conforming 
changes.</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Big Sky Energy Corporation is
filing this Amendment No. 2 to its Form 10-KSB for the following reason:</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:36pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Subsequent
to the issuance of the Company&#146;s 2004 financial statements, the 
Company&#146;s management determined that its belief that no obligation would 
exist to repay ABT Ltd. for costs they incurred or advanced to KoZhaN LLP in 
relation to the Morskoe oil field under the farm-out agreement signed October 
12, 2004 (see Note 10 of the Notes to the Amended and Restated Consolidated 
Financial Statements), should Ministry approval not be received on the transfer 
of 45% of the subsurface rights of the Morskoe licence to ABT Ltd., was 
incorrect, and that in fact an obligation would exist to repay ABT Ltd. for all 
costs incurred or advanced by them relating to the Morskoe oil field should 
Ministry approval not be received. &nbsp;As a result, the &#147;Short-Term 
Interest Free Loan from ABT LTD&#148; liability account, the &#147;Oil and Gas 
Properties&#148; asset account and the &#147;Other Current Asset&#148; account 
were understated in the
 amounts of $1,174,423, $1,088,263, and $86,160 respectively as previously 
reported on the Consolidated Balance Sheets included in the December 31, 2004 
Form 10-KSB. The error described above also resulted in an understatement in 
cash flow from financing activities in the amount of $334,000 and an 
overstatement in cash flow from investing activities in the amount of $334,000 
on the Consolidated Statements of Cash Flows. The Consolidated Balance Sheets 
and the Consolidated Statements of Cash Flows as at December 31, 2004 have been 
restated to correct these previous misstatements. &nbsp;<FONT FACE="Times">This 
restatement has no impact on earnings or equity.</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-14pt; line-height:14pt; font-
family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><B>ITEM 1. </B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:72pt; line-height:14pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman; font-size:12pt"><B>DESCRIPTION OF BUSINESS.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We are a development stage 
enterprise, which means we are in the process of developing our business. We 
commenced operations in 2000 as an Internet service provider in China. In fall
of 2003, we changed our focus to oil and gas exploration and production, seeking
to partner with China&#146;s national petroleum companies, at which time we 
changed our name to China Energy Ventures Corp. Through acquisition of other 
companies, in 2003 and 2004, we acquired five onshore licenses in the prolific 
pre-Caspian basin in the Republic of Kazakhstan. We determined to develop these 
blocks independently, by investing our capital or joint venturing with other 
companies. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">At the Annual General Meeting
of Shareholders held in Calgary, Alberta, December 3, 2004, shareholders 
approved changing the corporate name to Big Sky Energy Corporation, to reflect 
the changed nature of the business of the Corporation. Shareholders also elected
three new directors, each of which have extensive business and finance 
experience in the Republic of Kazakhstan. Three directors, whose extensive 
business experience is primarily focused in China, did not stand for re-election
to the Board of Directors. Throughout this document we use the 
&#147;Corporation&#148; to denote the single legal entity unless the context 
requires otherwise.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In December 2004, we sold our
100% shareholding in Big Sky Network Canada Ltd., which held our remaining 
assets in China, Big Sky Chengdu Technology Services Ltd, 100% owned, and our 
interest in the Sichuan Huayu Big Sky Network Ltd. joint venture, 50% owned. 
With this sale, we exited the Internet business in China. The sale of Big Sky 
Network Canada Ltd. is presented as a discontinued operation in our financial 
statements.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In January 2005, we commenced
negotiations with Mr. S.A. (Al) Sehsuvaroglu to secure his services as our 
president. A contract was signed with Mr. Sehsuvaroglu and he assumed his new 
position on March 1, 2005. We also signed a contract with Mr. Ruslan Tsarni, who
joined the Corporation as Vice-President, Business Development on March 15, 
2005.</P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>2</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We have incurred losses since
inception and we anticipate that we will continue to incur losses in the 
foreseeable future. Energy exploration and development entails significant risk 
&nbsp;(see&#148; Risk Factors&#148;) that impact the sustainability of early 
stage development companies. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We have successfully raised 
new equity capital for new business ventures but may not be able to do so in the
future. We are seeking to acquire producing oil and gas assets and to develop 
our own exploration potential. We will be unable to continue as a going concern 
if we are unable to earn sufficient revenues from our operations or raise 
additional capital through debt or equity financings to meet our working capital
and joint venture capital contribution obligations. &nbsp;Recent private 
placements have raised sufficient additional capital to meet our obligations 
until December 31, 2006. Furthermore, we expect to acquire at least one oil-
producing asset in 2005, using equity and debt to ensure sustainable operations 
in the future.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OVERVIEW OF CORPORATE
STRUCTURE</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We were incorporated in 
February 1993 as Institute for Counseling, Inc. under the laws of the State of 
Nevada. &nbsp;On April 14, 2000, we acquired China Broadband (BVI) Corp., a 
British Virgin Islands company incorporated in February 2000, by issuing 
13,500,000 shares of our common stock in exchange for all of the issued and 
outstanding common stock of China Broadband (BVI) Corp. &nbsp;The former 
shareholders of China Broadband (BVI) Corp. became our controlling shareholders.
&nbsp;On April 14, 2000, subsequent to the above acquisition, we changed our 
name to &quot;China Broadband Corp.&quot; and merged China Broadband (BVI) Corp.
into China Broadband Corp. Our principal executive office is located at Suite 
750, 440 &#150; 2<SUP>nd</SUP> Avenue SW, Calgary, Alberta, Canada T2P 5E9, and 
our phone number there is 1-403-234-8282. Our principal business office, in 
Kazakhstan, is located in a recently constructed office tower in central Almaty 
at Suite 3, 132 Do
styk Avenue, Almaty, Kazakhstan 650051, and our phone number there is 7 3272 628
394. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<A NAME="OLE_LINK2"></A><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We 
maintain a representative office in China at 1003 W2 Oriental Plaza, #1 East 
Chang An Avenue, Beijing, Peoples Republic of China 100738 and our phone number 
there is 86 10 8518 2686.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We maintain a World Wide Web 
site address at www.bigskycanada.com. Information on our web site is not part of
this document.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July 8, 2000, Big Sky 
Network Ltd. and Chengdu Huayu Information Co. Ltd. entered into a cooperative 
joint venture contract to form a joint venture company, Sichuan Huayu Big Sky 
Network Ltd., referred to as our Chengdu joint venture, under the laws of the 
People's Republic of China on Cooperative Joint Ventures using Chinese Foreign 
Investment. &nbsp;We had agreed to provide up to $5,500,000 in financing for the
joint venture, in the form of cash and equipment. &nbsp;The Chengdu joint 
venture was granted the exclusive right to provide equipment and technical 
services to our Chinese joint venture partner&#146;s subscribers to enable these
subscribers to access the Internet. Our Chinese joint venture partner failed to 
meet its obligations under the joint venture agreement. As we were unable to 
achieve a successful working partnership, the business of the joint venture was 
discontinued. After discussions and negotiations with the joint venture partner 
faile
d to achieve a satisfactory alternative, we commenced arbitration to seek 
damages. To date, such arbitration has not been successful. Although we sold 
this business in December 2004, we retain a 25% interest in any favorable 
settlement of this action. As the outcome of this arbitration is uncertain, we 
attribute no value to this residual interest.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We, through Big Sky Network 
Canada Ltd, (&#147;Big Sky Canada&#148;) held a 100% interest in Chengdu Big Sky
Network Technology Services Ltd., referred to as Chengdu Technology Services, 
which resells high-speed broadband Internet service to companies and residents 
in the section of Chengdu designated as a high technology park. As noted above, 
we sold our shareholding in Big Sky Canada on December 9, 2004 for $175,793.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Late in October 2003, we 
began investing in oil and gas assets, an area in which our management has 
knowledge and experience and it was our belief that it was the right time to 
diversify into the oil and natural gas industry. &nbsp;We considered that this 
diversification would provide us with a revenue stream and financial stability 
which would sustain our operations so that we could concentrate on growing our 
business in the oil and gas sector. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On October 27, 2003, the
Corporation entered into a Share Exchange Agreement with Big Sky Energy 
Kazakhstan Ltd. (&#147;BSEK&#148;), a private company incorporated in Alberta, 
Canada, and all its shareholders of record. &nbsp;Under the terms of the Share 
Exchange Agreement, we were required to issue up to a maximum of 8,000,000 
common shares in a share exchange offer with the shareholders of record of BSEK 
as of October 27, 2003. &nbsp;Management determined the net asset value per 
share and the </P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>3</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">number of shares to be issued based upon various criteria including a 
third party valuation. &nbsp;&nbsp;On January 12, 2004, we issued 8,000,000 of 
our common shares to the shareholders of BSEK in exchange for their shares in 
BSEK. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">BSEK has a 90% interest in 
KoZhaN LLP, (&#147;KoZhaN&#148;), a Republic of Kazakhstan limited liability 
partnership, which has three petroleum licenses in the Atyrau region of 
Kazakhstan.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December 29, 2003, we 
changed out name from China Broadband Corp. to China Energy Ventures Corp. On 
December 3, 2004 shareholders approved a further name change to Big Sky Energy 
Corporation.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On May 10, 2004, Big Sky 
Energy Atyrau Ltd., at that time a 75% owned subsidiary of Big Sky, 
(&#147;BSEA&#148;), purchased 100% of Vector Energy West LLP, a Kazakhstan 
limited liability partnership, (&#147;Vector&#148;), for $4,430,000. &nbsp;This 
purchase price was determined by a valuation of Vector&#146;s Atyrau and Liman-2
licenses which was performed by PetroGlobe (Canada) Ltd., an independent third 
party. On the same date, pursuant to the terms of an Agreement for Assignment of
the Creditor&#146;s Rights, BSEA paid $570,000 to Lorgate Management Inc. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July 6, 2004, we closed a 
private placement of $8,050,000 and issued 16,100,000 shares. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We currently have enough cash
on hand to cover the expected level of general and administrative and other 
overhead costs throughout 2006. We had originally assumed work commitments on 
our licenses in Kazakhstan, which would require expenditures estimated at up to 
$35 million, which may be decreased upon prior approval of the Kazakhstan 
competent authority to the commitments defined in the respective five 
hydrocarbon contracts to a total amount of approximately $16 million. Our 
commitments are measured in actual work completed, not in money expended. We can
successfully meet our work commitments for a lesser expenditure of money if we 
can perform the work more efficiently. Work commitments consist of well 
drilling, seismic shoots, data processing, workover and re-entry of existing 
wells and general business activity that serves to further develop, explore, 
produce and sell hydrocarbons in Kazakhstan. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Work program commitments for 
2004 have been completed only in part. To satisfy the Kazakh regulatory 
authorities the work commitments not completed in 2004 have to be completed in 
2005.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following figure sets 
forth our corporate structure as at December 31, 2004.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Neither Big Sky nor any of 
our subsidiaries have been subject to any bankruptcy, receivership or similar 
proceedings.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OVERVIEW OF BUSINESS 
STRATEGY</B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Oil
and Gas Business</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the last half of 2003,
we commenced the diversification of our efforts towards the exploration and 
exploitation of oil and gas in selected countries. &nbsp;Our objective is to 
find fields with proven reserves that justify exploration and that require some 
enhanced recovery, workover, additional drilling or stimulation, and that have 
an exploration upside, located near infrastructure and markets, in countries 
with favorable fiscal and tax regimes and well developed commercial laws, 
including adequate </P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>4</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">environmental regulations. We determined that Kazakhstan was one country 
that meets these criteria and commenced efforts to locate acquisition 
opportunities there.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Big Sky Energy 
Kazakhstan Ltd.</I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Big Sky Energy Kazakhstan 
Ltd. was incorporated on July 29, 2003 in Alberta, Canada and holds a 90% 
interest in KoZhaN, which has three petroleum licenses in the Atyrau region of 
Kazakhstan. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In late 2003 and early 2004, 
BSEK entered into various share purchase agreements with Shengli Oilfield Junwei
Petroleum-Tech Development Co. Ltd., a wholly owned subsidiary of Sinopec Corp. 
for an investment into BSEK of $10,000,000. &nbsp;We decided to pursue this 
project ourselves and on July 1, 2004, a Severance Agreement was completed by 
BSEK and Shengli that terminated all of the various share purchase agreements 
and BSEK repaid funds that had been received from Shengli. Management will 
consider other farm out options to third parties as opportunities arise.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On October 27, 2003, the 
Corporation entered into a Share Exchange Agreement with BSEK and all its 
shareholders of record. &nbsp;Under the terms of the Agreement, we forwarded 
$500,000 to BSEK as a short-term loan, which was to be repaid within 60 days. 
&nbsp;As well, we were required to issue up to a maximum of 8,000,000 common 
shares in a share exchange offer with the shareholders of record of BSEK as of 
October 27, 2003. &nbsp;Management determined the net asset value per share and 
the number of shares to be issued based upon various criteria including a
valuation performed by PetroGlobe (Canada) Ltd., a third party independent 
petroleum engineering firm. In December 2003, we forwarded an additional 
$625,000 to BSEK as a short-term loan, which was to be repaid within 60 days. On
January 12, 2004, we issued 8,000,000 of our common shares to the shareholders 
of BSEK in exchange for their shares in BSEK thereby giving us 100% ownership of
BSEK. &nbsp;On Janu
ary 14, 2004, BSEK made a payment of $250,000 on the initial loan made in 
October 2003. On January 20, 2004, we extended the repayment terms on both loans
to BSEK to June 1, 2004 and set the interest rate at 5% per annum. &nbsp;As of 
December 31, 2004, these loans had not been repaid. &nbsp;BSEK will repay them 
once it has started production. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mr. Matthew Heysel, who is a 
shareholder, Chairman and Chief Executive Officer of the Corporation; was 
Chairman and Chief Executive Officer of BSEK and also the Vice-Chairman of 
KoZhaN at the time of the Share Exchange Agreement with BSEK. &nbsp;Mr. Heysel, 
as a board member of the Corporation and BSEK, voluntarily abstained from voting
on the transaction with BSEK. &nbsp;Mr. Heysel continues to hold his 
directorships with these entities, but has relinquished his Chief Executive 
Officer designation to Mr. Sehsuvaroglu.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mr. Daming Yang, who is a 
shareholder and director of the Corporation, was the President and a director of
BSEK and also the Chairman of KoZhaN at the time of the Share Exchange Agreement
with BSEK. &nbsp;Mr. Yang, as a board member of the Corporation and BSEK, 
voluntarily abstained from voting on the transaction with BSEK. Mr. Yang 
continues to hold his directorships and offices with these entities.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:36pt; text-indent:36pt; font-family:Times New
Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mr. Kai Yang, at the time of 
the Share Exchange Agreement with BSEK, was a major shareholder of the 
Corporation, the sole shareholder of Big Sky Energy Canada Ltd., which held 80% 
of the stock of BSEK and Mr. Daming Yang&#146;s brother. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&nbsp;On February 27, 2004, 
the Corporation entered into an Asset Purchase Agreement with IbrizOil Inc., an 
Alberta corporation, hereinafter referred to as Ibriz. &nbsp;Under the terms of 
the agreement, Ibriz assigned its 5% over-riding royalty in BSEK&#146;s interest
in KoZhaN in exchange for common stock of the Corporation. &nbsp;The value of 
the royalty held in Ibriz was determined using the results of the valuation 
report performed by PetroGlobe (Canada) Ltd., an independent third party, in 
connection with the Share Purchase Agreement entered into by the Corporation and
BSEK on October 27, 2003. &nbsp;The amount of common stock issued was determined
using the average closing price of our common stock for the five days prior to 
February 27, 2004. &nbsp;On March 4, 2004, we issued 681,475 common shares to 
Ibriz in connection with the agreement. At the time of this transaction, Mr. Van
Doorne was our Executive Vice President, the Managing Director of BSEK a
nd a shareholder of the Corporation, as well as, the Chief Executive Officer, a 
director and a shareholder of Ibriz. On March 18, 2005, Mr. Van Doorne resigned 
as Chief Executive Officer and a director of Ibriz.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; padding-left:36pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:12pt"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>KoZhaN </I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">KoZhaN was incorporated as a 
limited liability partnership on April 28, 2001 in the Republic of Kazakhstan by
five Kazakhstani nationals unrelated to us.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On February 17, 2003, KoZhaN 
entered into agreements with the Government of Kazakhstan for the exploration 
and development of three petroleum licenses in the Atyrau region of western 
Kazakhstan.</P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>5</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<TABLE style="page-break-before:always" cellspacing=0><TR><BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<TD valign=top width=24><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">-</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=619.2><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">The Morskoe license covers an area of 18,434 acres. &nbsp;The Morskoe 
field was discovered in 1965 . &nbsp;In 1965, five wells were drilled in the 
field, resulting in four oil wells. &nbsp;One well tested a combined oil flow of
1300 barrels of oil per day (&#147;bopd&#148;). &nbsp;The wells were shut-in and
have never produced oil. </P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top width=24><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">-
</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=619.2><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">The Karatal license, which covers an area of 103,982 acres. &nbsp;Several
wells drilled in the late 1960s on the property tested small oil flows. </P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top width=24><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">-
</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=619.2><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">The Dauletaly license covers an area of 33,359 acres. &nbsp;No reserves 
have been established on the license, which is adjacent to the Krykmyltyk field,
which is currently producing approximately 2,000 bopd.</P>
</TD></TR>
</TABLE>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In August 2003, in an arms-
length transaction, the five shareholders of KoZhaN, each holding a 20% interest
in KoZhaN, entered into a Sale and Purchase Agreement with BSEK whereby BSEK 
purchased a 90% interest in KoZhaN for future consideration based upon the 
achievement of KoZhaN production milestones. &nbsp;BSEK entered into this 
agreement in order to obtain the contractual rights for exploration and 
development for the Morskoe, Karatal and Dauletaly fields owned by KoZhaN. BSEK 
currently owns a 90% interest in KoZhaN and the remaining five shareholders each
own a 2% interest. &nbsp;BSEK is required to make the following payments to the 
five shareholders, as a group, upon KoZhaN achieving the following 
milestones:</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<TABLE cellspacing=0><TR><TD valign=top width=24><P style="margin:0pt; font-

Roman">$100,000 after the receipt by KoZhaN of payment in full for two sales of 
a commercial quantity of oil produced, saved, marketed and sold by KoZhaN. 
&nbsp;Each sale shall not be of less than 4,000 tonnes of oil and shall be 
calculated after deducting the government&#146;s share of production, if 
any.</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top width=24><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">-
</P>

production of 40,000 tonnes of a commercial quantity of oil produced, saved, 
marketed and sold by KoZhaN. &nbsp;The 40,000 tonnes shall be calculated after 
deducting the government&#146;s share of production, if any.</P>

</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=619.2><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">A quarterly payment per barrel of oil produced, saved, marketed and sold 
by KoZhaN (&#147;Production Payment&#148;). &nbsp;Such production is to be 
calculated after deducting the government&#146;s share of production, if any. 
The Production Payment shall equal $0.35 per barrel if the price of oil is equal
to or less than $14.00, $0.75 per barrel if the price of oil is greater than 
$14.00 and less than or equal to $18.00, $1.00 per barrel if the price of oil is
greater than $18.00 and less than or equal to $22.00, or $1.50 per barrel if the
price of oil is greater than $22.00. &nbsp;The price of oil shall be determined 
as a quarterly average based on a calendar year and calculated based on the 
actual value of oil realized by sale of the oil, net of transportation and 
tariff costs.</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top width=24><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">-
</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=619.2><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New

Contract Territories, KoZhaN shall pay a bonus of $0.05 multiplied by the number
of barrels of oil attributed to the oilfield reserves associated with that award
as defined in State Balance of Reserves (Oil) of Kazakhstan as of January 1, 
2000. &nbsp;Payment of the bonus shall be made within 30 days of the tender 
being awarded.</P>
</TD></TR>

<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><B><I>Big Sky Energy Atyrau Ltd.</I></B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Big 
Sky Energy Atyrau Ltd. was incorporated on April 8, 2004 in Alberta, Canada. 
&nbsp;Initially, we owned 75% of this subsidiary and Fullup Limited, a Cypriot 
registered corporation, owned 25%. &nbsp;&nbsp;We entered into this corporate 
arrangement with Fullup Limited based upon representations from it that it would
be able to present us with oil and gas opportunities in the Atyrau area of 
western Kazakhstan. </P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New Roman">As 
consideration for facilitation of the successful acquisition of Vector, BSEA 
granted a royalty to Fullup Limited of $1.00 per barrel on oil sold by Vector 
from the Atyrau and Liman-2 licenses. On November 10, 2004, BSEA and Fullup 
Limited entered </P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>6</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-
family:Times New Roman">into a Share Exchange Agreement whereby Fullup Limited 
agreed to exchange its 25% interest in BSEA for 3,500,000 common shares of the 
Corporation.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><B><I>Vector Energy West </I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Vector Energy West was 
incorporated as a limited liability partnership in the Republic of Kazakhstan on
July 4, 2001.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December 28, 2002, Vector 
Energy entered into agreements with the Government of Kazakhstan for the 
exploration and development of two petroleum licenses in western Kazakhstan.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<TABLE cellspacing=0><TR><TD valign=top width=23.933><P style="margin:0pt; font-
family:Times New Roman">-</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=612.067><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">The Atyrau license covers an area of 2,599,044 acres. &nbsp;The Atyrau 
field is located on the north shore of the Caspian Sea, near the city of Atyrau.
&nbsp;This block has some 33 salt domes identified by seismic. Of these, 8 post 
salt prospects have been identified and drilled. &nbsp;</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top width=23.933><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">-</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=612.067><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">The Liman-2 license covers an area of 1,015,599 acres. &nbsp;The Liman-2 
field is located immediately west of the Atyrau license on the north shore of 
the Caspian Sea. &nbsp;This block has some 10 un-drilled salt domes. &nbsp;</P>
</TD></TR>
</TABLE>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">&nbsp;On June 1, 2004, Vector granted a royalty of $1.00 per barrel of 
oil sold by Vector from the Atyrau and Liman-2 licenses to the former President 
of Vector. This royalty expires June 1, 2005.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><B><I>Big Sky Energy Ltd.</I></B></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Big 
Sky Energy Ltd. was incorporated on May 31, 2004 in Alberta, Canada in order to 
have a representative oil and natural gas office in China. &nbsp;We own 100% of 
this subsidiary, which is currently inactive.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:5pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Oil and Gas 
Business</I></B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In Kazakhstan, producers have
the right to negotiate sales contracts directly with purchasers, allowing the 
market to determine the price of oil. &nbsp;Under the terms of the three 
Contracts for Exploration and Production of Hydrocarbons (&#147;Hydrocarbon 
Contracts&#148;) entered into by the Ministry of Energy and Mineral Resources of
the Republic of Kazakhstan and KoZhaN on the Morskoe, Karatal and Dauletaly 
Fields, referred to as the Hydrocarbon Contracts, all production has to be sold 
into the domestic market during the Exploration Phase of the Hydrocarbon 
Contracts. The Exploration Phase has a maximum term of 6 years. &nbsp;We have
the right to accelerate the exploration activities and thus shorten the 
exploration phase. &nbsp;During the Exploitation Phase we can sell up to 80% of 
our production on the international markets. &nbsp;Currently domestic prices are
approximately US$145 per tonne. If the domestic market cannot absorb the 
produced hydrocarbons
 we can sell our product on the international market. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Competition </B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Several domestic and 
international companies operate in Kazakhstan. &nbsp;The Government of 
Kazakhstan issues licenses on a regular basis through bidding rounds. 
&nbsp;Shares in existing licenses can be freely sold and purchased, subject to 
the terms of the individual Charter and Foundation Agreements in place. 
&nbsp;Late in 2004, the Government of Kazakhstan passed legislation providing 
certain pre-emptive rights whereby the government has the right to acquire 
interests in fields if there is an intention of the license holder to sell or 
farm out to a third party. However, there is little competition from foreign 
companies for the assets targeted in Kazakhstan by us. &nbsp;Major international
companies target the large high-risk offshore blocks in the Caspian Sea.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Local refineries are 
generally amply supplied by existing producers. &nbsp;Although we are required 
to sell our crude into the local markets, we can sell our produced hydrocarbons 
into the international markets if the refineries are not capable of accepting 
our production. &nbsp;There are no restrictions to access the pipelines 
exporting crude from Kazakhstan, except that a transportation agreement has to 
be signed with KazTransOil and export quotes have to be obtained from the 
Ministry of Energy.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Employees and 
Consultants</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">As the focus of business of 
the Corporation centers in Kazakhstan, more of the officers and management will 
be located in the Almaty office. Beginning with our President, we expect to 
operate our business from Almaty. Field operations personnel will work from an 
office in Atyrau or will be located at various field work sites.</P>

size:8pt" align=center>7</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">Vector and KoZhaN engage local staff as required to manage their 
business. &nbsp;We anticipate that Big Sky and our subsidiaries, on an as-needed
basis, will hire additional employees over the next fiscal year. We are 
consolidating our two offices in Almaty. Set forth below is an indication of 
current operations and the numbers of employees and consultants required by our 
subsidiaries and us to maintain current operations, as at March 31, 2005:</P>

<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman" align=justify>Should our 
development necessitate, we will hire additional employees and consultants in 
sales, marketing, and administration over the current fiscal year and will hire 
additional management and employees on an as-needed basis. &nbsp;If the need 
arises for additional technical employees and we are unable to hire qualified 
employees in a timely manner, we may outsource projects to third parties.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>ADDITIONAL FACTORS THAT 
MAY AFFECT FUTURE RESULTS </B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">An investment in our common
stock involves a high degree of risk. You should read the following risk factors
carefully before purchasing our common stock. We believe that these represent 
all the current material risk factors that may affect our business. &nbsp;If any
of the risks discussed below actually occur, our business, financial condition, 
operating results or cash flows could be materially adversely affected. This 
could cause the trading price of our common stock to decline.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Risks Relating To Our 
Business</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>We have a limited 
operating history and have changed the focus of our operations by entering into 
the oil and gas industry. &nbsp;The failure of our plans could ultimately force 
us to reduce or suspend operations and even liquidate our assets and wind-up and
dissolve our company.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We have a limited operating 
history, a history of minimal revenues and a history of losses. &nbsp;We began 
our business activities in April 2000 in China. &nbsp;Our operations in the 
Chinese Internet market produced only minimal revenues and we have divested this
business, effective December 9, 2004. We have diversified our operations to oil 
and natural gas exploration and production, an area in which our management has 
been successful in past endeavors, although we do not know if Big Sky will be 
successful in any of these plans due to our early stage of operations in the oil
and gas industry.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>We have incurred net 
losses since inception and anticipate that losses will continue. Should losses 
continue indefinitely, it would eventually result in us ceasing 
operations.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We have incurred losses since
inception and had an accumulated deficit of $30,185,135 at December 31, 2004. We
anticipate that we will continue to incur net losses due to an increased level 
of planned operating and capital expenditures, increased sales and marketing 
costs, high costs associated with oil and gas exploration and development, 
additional personnel requirements and our general growth objectives. &nbsp;We 
anticipate that our net losses will increase in the near future as we implement 
our business strategy and commence oil and gas exploration. &nbsp;Our ability to
earn a profit will depend on the success of our oil and gas exploration and 
development programs, which has not yet been achieved. &nbsp;We may never 
achieve profitability. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Our ability to continue as
a going concern requires us to raise additional funds and produce working 
capital from oil and gas operations.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In light of our lack of 
profitability and the risks described in this section, our management and our 
independent registered chartered accountants have expressed substantial doubt as
to our ability to continue as a going concern. &nbsp;&nbsp;At December 31, 2004,
we had net working capital deficiency of $2,793,503. &nbsp;We will need 
additional capital or a farmout of our interests to third parties to fund any 
new ventures, which is uncertain and will likely result in the dilution to 
existing shareholders&#146; interests. </P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>8</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><I>Our inability to retain our key managerial personnel could affect our 
ability to continue conducting our business.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our success depends to a 
significant extent on the continued efforts of our executive officers, 
principally Messrs. Heysel, Sehsuvaroglu and Tsarni, who are responsible for the
continuing development of our oil and gas assets. The loss of any one of these 
individuals could have a material adverse effect on our ability to continue to 
locate, negotiate and acquire oil and gas assets and financing to develop these 
assets. We would have to replace any such individuals with someone that has 
commensurate experience abilities if they were to leave us. We have entered into
employment and non-competition agreements with all of these individuals.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Our business may be 
adversely affected by relationships between the United States and the countries 
in which we do business, which may impede our ability to operate in the 
countries in which we are located.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We are a Nevada corporation 
and subject to the laws of the United States. &nbsp;Our principal businesses are
conducted through wholly-owned subsidiaries that operate in Kazakhstan. 
&nbsp;Our business is directly affected by political and economic conditions in 
Kazakhstan. &nbsp;Our business may be adversely affected by the diplomatic and 
political relationships between the U.S., China, Russia and Kazakhstan. 
&nbsp;These relationships may adversely influence the Kazakhstan government and 
public opinion of U.S. corporations conducting business in Kazakhstan and may 
affect our ability to obtain regulatory approval to operate effectively. 
&nbsp;In addition, boycotts, protests, governmental sanctions and other actions 
could adversely affect our ability to operate profitably.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Risks Related to Our Oil 
and Gas Operations</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>If our exploration and 
development programs prove unsuccessful, we may not be able to continue 
operations.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">An investment in our company 
should be considered highly speculative due to the nature of our involvement in 
the exploration, development and production of oil and natural gas. &nbsp;Oil 
and gas exploration involves a high degree of risk, which even a combination of 
experience, knowledge and careful evaluation may not be able to overcome. 
&nbsp;Exploratory drilling is subject to numerous risks, including the risk that
no commercially productive oil and natural gas reservoirs will be encountered. 
&nbsp;The cost to drill, complete and operate wells is often uncertain, and 
drilling operations may be curtailed, delayed or cancelled as a result of a 
variety of factors including unexpected drilling conditions, abnormal pressures,
equipment failures, premature declines of reservoirs, blow-outs, sour gas 
releases, fires, spills or other accidents, as well as weather conditions, 
compliance with governmental requirements, delays in receiving governmental 
approvals or 
permits, unexpected environmental issues and shortages or delays in the delivery
of equipment. &nbsp;Our inability to drill wells that produce commercial 
quantities of oil and natural gas would have a material adverse effect on our 
business, financial condition and results of operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Future oil and gas 
exploration may involve unprofitable efforts, not only from dry wells, but from 
wells that are productive but do not produce sufficient net revenues to return a
profit after exploration, drilling, operating and other costs. &nbsp;Completion 
of wells does not ensure a profit on the investment or recovery of exploration, 
drilling, completion and operating costs. &nbsp;Drilling hazards or
environmental damage could greatly increase the cost of operations, and various 
field operating conditions may adversely affect production. &nbsp;Adverse 
conditions include delays in obtaining governmental approvals or consents, shut-
ins of connected wells resulting from extreme weather conditions, insufficient 
storage or transportation capacity or other geological and mechanical 
conditions.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Fluctuations in commodity 
prices could have a material impact on our revenues, which would affect our 
profitability.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Commodity price risk related 
to conventional crude oil prices could become our most significant market risk 
exposure if we achieve oil and natural gas production. &nbsp;Crude oil prices 
are influenced by such worldwide factors as the Organization of the Petroleum 
Exporting Countries actions, political events and supply and demand 
fundamentals. &nbsp;At this time, we cannot accurately predict these 
fluctuations because we do not know when we will commence generating revenues 
from our oil and gas operations. &nbsp;Furthermore, we cannot estimate, at this 
time, the impact of commodity price fluctuations until we can predict the level 
of revenues.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Application, 
interpretation and enforcement of government taxes is inconsistent making it 
difficult for us to ensure that we are compliant which could lead to 
penalties.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The tax environment in 
Kazakhstan is subject to change, inconsistent application, interpretation and 
enforcement. &nbsp;Non-compliance with Kazakhstan laws and regulations can lead 
to the imposition of penalties and interest. &nbsp;We intend to make every 
effort to conform to these laws and regulations. However, our interpretations 
and those of our advisors may not be the same as those of government officials, 
which could lead to penalties and interest.</P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>9</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Vector and KoZhaN face 
competition which could adversely affect their ability to penetrate the oil and 
gas market in Kazakhstan which may make it difficult to attain profitability. 
</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The oil and gas market is 
competitive and some of the competitors of Vector and KoZhaN are major 
international energy industry operators.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">These competitors have 
various advantages over Vector and KoZhaN, including:</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<TABLE cellspacing=0><TR><TD valign=top width=23.533><P style="margin:0pt; font-
family:Times New Roman">-</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=571.667><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">substantially greater financial resources, which gives them greater 
flexibility when developing their exploration and drilling programs;</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top width=23.533><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">-</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=571.667><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">greater recognition in the industry, which influences a potential 
partners&#146; decision to participate in programs;</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top width=23.533><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">-</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=571.667><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">larger operations, which provides economies of scale and operating 
efficiencies not available to Vector or KoZhaN;</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top width=23.533><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">-</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=571.667><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">longer operating histories; and</P>
</TD></TR>
<TR><TD valign=top width=23.533><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">-</P>
</TD><TD valign=top width=571.667><P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman">more established relationships with government officials and other 
strategic partners.</P>
</TD></TR>
</TABLE>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Vector and KoZhaN may be 
unable to successfully compete with these established competitors, which may 
adversely affect their ability to acquire Hydrocarbon Contracts, licenses and 
drilling permits, which could impact their ability to generate revenue. 
&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Compliance, interpretation
and enforcement with evolving environmental laws and regulations may impact our 
expenses in a negative manner, which would directly impact our profit 
margins.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Extensive national, regional 
and local environmental laws and regulations in Kazakhstan affect the operations
of Vector and KoZhaN. &nbsp;These laws and regulations set various standards 
regulating certain aspects of health and environmental quality which provide for
user fees, penalties and other liabilities for the violation of these standards 
and establish, in some circumstances, obligations to remediate current and 
former facilities and off-site locations. We believe we are currently in 
compliance with all existing Kazakhstan environmental laws and regulations. 
&nbsp;However, as new environmental laws and legislation are enacted and the old
laws are repealed, interpretation, application and enforcement of the laws may 
become inconsistent. &nbsp;Compliance in the future could require significant 
expenditures, which would directly impact our profit margins.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>If Vector and KoZhaN 
repeatedly do not honor their capital expenditure commitments with the Republic 
of Kazakhstan, they may lose their exploration licenses.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Pursuant to the three 
Hydrocarbon Contracts, a commitment was made by KoZhaN to invest, in Kazakhstan,
an aggregate of $16.43 million in capital expenditures, investments or other 
items that may be treated as capital assets of KoZhaN on or before December 31, 
2009. KoZhaN has commenced this investment using loans from BSEK and intends to 
fund this investment using further loans from BSEK and, in the long term, from 
future production revenues. &nbsp;These expenditures will be used to further 
exploit and develop existing fields and to explore for additional reserves to 
enhance future production and revenues. &nbsp;If the required investment is not 
made within the agreed time period, KoZhaN may lose its exploration licenses. 
&nbsp;If the exploration effort is unsuccessful or future exploration is
determined to be not profitable, KoZhaN can elect not to invest the balance of 
the required exploration investment. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Pursuant to the Liman-2 and 
Atyrau Hydrocarbon Contracts, Vector has committed to invest for its two 
exploration assets an aggregate of $53.9 million in capital expenditures, 
investments or other items that may be treated as capital assets of Vector on or
before December 31, 2007. Vector has funded its operations using loans from its 
parent company and will further finance its subsoil use activities using funds 
of its parent company and further production revenues. If the required capital 
investment commitments are not met within the agreed exploration period, Vector 
may lose its exploration licenses. If the exploration effort is unsuccessful or 
future exploration is determined to be not profitable, Vector may withdraw from 
the Hydrocarbon Contracts without investing the balance of the required 
exploration investment.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&nbsp;</P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>10</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><I>We may suffer currency exchange losses if the Tenge depreciates 
relative to the U.S. dollar. </I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We report in U.S. Dollars. 
&nbsp;Anticipated early oil production will likely be sold on the domestic 
market where selling prices are determined in the Tenge, the currency of 
Kazakhstan. &nbsp;The majority of our Kazakhstan operating costs will be 
denominated in Tenge. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Should we become 
profitable, we will be subject to Kazakhstan&#146;s Excess Profits Tax, which 
would reduce our profit margin.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Through our Kazakhstan 
subsidiaries, we may become subject to Excess Profits Tax under the terms of the
Hydrocarbon Contracts they have for oil and natural gas exploration and 
production. &nbsp;&nbsp;Excess Profits Tax is in addition to statutory income 
taxes and takes effect after the field has achieved a cumulative internal rate 
of return higher than 20%. &nbsp;The Excess Profits Tax ranges from 0% to 60% of
taxable income. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Other Risks</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Our shareholders may not 
be able to enforce U.S. civil liabilities claims thereby limiting their ability 
to collect on claims against us.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our assets are located 
outside the United States and are held through wholly owned subsidiaries 
incorporated under the laws of &nbsp;Canada and Kazakhstan. &nbsp;Our current 
operations are conducted in Kazakhstan. &nbsp;In addition, our directors and 
officers are nationals and/or residents of countries other than the United 
States. &nbsp;All or a substantial portion of the assets of these persons are 
located outside the United States. &nbsp;As a result, it may be difficult for 
you to effect service of process within the United States upon these persons. 
&nbsp;In addition, there is uncertainty as to whether the courts of &nbsp;Canada
or Kazakhstan would recognize or enforce judgments of United States courts
obtained against us or such persons predicated upon the civil liability 
provisions of the securities laws of the United States or any state thereof, or 
be competent to hear original actions brought in these countries against us or 
such persons predicated u
pon the securities laws of the United States or any state thereof.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Broker-dealers may be 
discouraged from effecting transactions in our shares because they are 
considered penny stocks and are subject to the penny stock rules thereby 
potentially limiting the liquidity of our shares.</I></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Rules&nbsp;15g-1 through 15g-
9 promulgated under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, impose 
sales practice and disclosure requirements on NASD broker-dealers who make a 
market in &quot;penny stocks&quot;. A penny stock generally includes any non-
NASDAQ equity security that has a market price of less than $5.00 per share. 
&nbsp;Our shares are quoted on the OTC/BB, and the price of our shares ranged 
from $0.01 (low) to $10.00 (high) during the period from September 25, 2000 to 
March 31, 2005. &nbsp;The closing price of our shares on March 31, 2005 was 
$1.12. &nbsp;NASD broker-dealers who act as market makers for our shares 
generally facilitate purchases and sales of our shares. &nbsp;The additional 
sales practice and disclosure requirements imposed upon broker-dealers may 
discourage broker-dealers from effecting transactions in our shares, which could
severely limit the market liquidity of the shares and impede the sale of our 
shares in the second
ary market.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Under the penny stock 
regulations, a broker-dealer selling penny stock to anyone other than an 
established customer or &quot;accredited investor&quot; (generally, an 
individual with net worth in excess of $1,000,000 or an annual income exceeding 
$200,000, or $300,000 together with his or her spouse) must make a special 
suitability determination for the purchaser and must receive the purchaser's 
written consent to the transaction prior to sale, unless the broker-dealer or 
the transaction is otherwise exempt.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In addition, the penny stock 
regulations require the broker-dealer to deliver, prior to any transaction 
involving a penny stock, a disclosure schedule prepared by the SEC relating to 
the penny stock market, unless the broker-dealer or the transaction is otherwise
exempt. &nbsp;A broker-dealer is also required to disclose commissions payable 
to the broker-dealer and the registered representative and current quotations 
for the securities. &nbsp;Finally, a broker-dealer is required to send monthly 
statements disclosing recent price information with respect to the penny stock 
held in a customer's account and information with respect to the limited market 
in penny stocks.</P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>11</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-14pt; line-
height:14pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><B>ITEM 2. </B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:72pt; line-height:14pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman; font-size:12pt"><B>DESCRIPTION OF PROPERTY.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&nbsp;Our principal 
Kazakhstan business office is located at Suite 3, 132 Dostyk Avenue, Almaty, 
Kazakhstan 650051. The office consists of approximately 4,000 square feet of 
office space held under a lease that expires November 30, 2005. We intend to
renew this lease for the foreseeable future. Monthly rental cost for this space 
is approximately 1 million Tenge, approximately US$7,700. This is also the 
registered office for Vector.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our principal executive 
office and our offices of BSEK and BSEA are located at Suite 750, 440 &#150; 
2<SUP>nd</SUP> Avenue SW., Calgary, Alberta, Canada, T2P 5E9 and consists of 
approximately 4,000 square feet of office space held under a lease that expires 
on May 30, 2007 subject to certain early termination provisions after one year. 
&nbsp;The monthly rental cost of this space is Cdn.$10,308, plus variable 
operating costs. </P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">KoZhaN has an office located 
at 1/1 Dzhandosov Street, Almaty, 480008, Kazakhstan and consists of 
approximately 590 square feet of office space held under a lease that expires on
June 30, 2005 at a monthly rental cost of $3,000. The lease is renewable for 
consecutive three-month periods. &nbsp;We plan to discontinue this lease in the 
near future.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our Beijing representative 
office is located at 1003 W2 Oriental Plaza, #1 East Chang An Avenue, Beijing, 
Peoples Republic of China 100738. The office consists of 197 square metres, 
approximately 1200 square feet, held under a lease that expires February 28, 
2006 at a monthly rent of $4,925 plus management fees.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OIL AND GAS 
PROPERTIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Morskoe License</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Morskoe License is 
located near Tengiz in western Kazakhstan, about 90 kilometers southwest of 
Kulsary railway station. &nbsp;Neighboring producing oilfields include Tengiz 10
miles to the northeast and Prorva, 10 miles to the south. &nbsp;The field was 
identified by seismic investigation in 1963 and proven through drilling in 1965.
&nbsp;It shows the anticlinal structures draped over the top of the salt dome 
and delineated to the northwest by a fault. &nbsp;The oil-bearing horizons 
belong to the Lower Cretaceous Series at a depth of 4,000 feet.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The oil has been trapped in 
sandstones with a porosity exceeding 20%. &nbsp;Net pays of over 20 feet have 
been established. &nbsp;Three wells are prime candidates for re-completion, 
having tested oil at combined rates of over 1,000 bopd. &nbsp;The quality of the
crude ranges from 35<FONT FACE="Symbol">&#176;</FONT> to 25<FONT 
FACE="Symbol">&#176;</FONT> American Petroleum Institute (&#147;API&#148;). 
&nbsp;The License has an area of 18,434 acres. &nbsp;We have the rights from 
surface to the Lower Permian.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Karatal License</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Karatal License is 
located near Makat in western Kazakhstan, about 50 miles north of Atyrau, 
western Kazakhstan&#146;s major city. &nbsp;All large North American and 
European service companies are operating out of Atyrau. &nbsp;Neighboring 
producing oilfields include Daraimola 10 miles to the northwest and Tanatar, 5 
miles to the east. &nbsp;The field was identified by seismic investigation in 
1958 and proven through drilling in 1959. &nbsp;It shows several anticlinal 
structures draped over the top of salt domes and delineated by faults. &nbsp;The
oil-bearing horizons belong to the Lower Cretaceous Series at depths between 300
and 3,000 feet. &nbsp;The oil has been trapped in sandstones with a porosity 
exceeding 20%. &nbsp;Two wells are prime candidates for re-completion, having 
tested small amounts of oil. &nbsp;Although some oil production has been 
established, the license is considered an exploration block.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The License has an area of 
103,982 acres. &nbsp;We have the rights from surface to the basement. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Dauletaly License</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Dauletaly License is 
located near Emba in western Kazakhstan, about 60 miles northeast of Kulsary. 
&nbsp;Neighboring producing oilfields include Krykmyltyk 1 mile to the north and
Zhubantam, 10 miles to the east. &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;It shows several typical 
anticlinal structures draped over the top of salt domes and delineated by 
faults. &nbsp;The license is considered an exploration block, with substantial 
deep potential, based on regional maps.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The License has an area of 
33,359 acres. &nbsp;We have the rights from surface to the basement.</P>
<BR>

<BR>
<BR>
<P style="margin:0pt; line-height:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-
size:8pt" align=center>12</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><BR></P>
<BR>
<BR>
<BR>
<P style="page-break-before:always; margin:0pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Atyrau and Liman-2 
Licenses</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December 28, 2002, Vector 
entered into a Hydrocarbon Contractor contract with the Government of the 
Republic of Kazakhstan to explore for and produce hydrocarbons in the Atyrau and
Liman-2 oilfields in the Atyrau region. From that date to December 31, 2003, no 
major exploration activities have been carried out. In accordance with the 
Hydrocarbon Contract &nbsp;#1077, dated December 28, 2002. Vector received the 
right to perform exploration activities on the Atyrau oilfield during 6 years 
from 2003 to 2008. In accordance with the Hydrocarbon Contract dated December 
28, 2002, Vector received the right to perform exploration activities on the 
Liman-2 oilfield during 5 years from, 2003 to 2007 inclusive and to perform 
production activities during the subsequent 20 years.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-14pt; line-height:14pt; font-
family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><B>ITEM 3. </B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:72pt; line-height:14pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman; font-size:12pt"><B>LEGAL PROCEEDINGS.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">To our knowledge, neither Big
Sky nor any of our officers or directors is a party to any material legal 
proceeding or litigation and such persons know of no material legal proceeding 
or contemplated or threatened litigation and none of our officers or directors 
have been found by any court of competent jurisdiction to have violated any 
federal or state securities or commodities law. There are no judgments, orders, 
or decrees against us or our officers or directors that limit in any manner our 
involvement or that of our officers or directors in any type of business, 
securities or banking activities. None of our officers or directors has been 
convicted of a felony or misdemeanor relating to securities or performance in 
corporate office. &nbsp;None of our officers or directors has been involved in 
any capacity in any bankruptcy petition. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We are subject to potential 
litigation in the normal course of operations. &nbsp;There are no claims 
currently pending that we consider would materially affect our operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<A NAME="node4"></A><P style="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:-14pt; line-
height:14pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:12pt"><B>ITEM 4. </B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:72pt; line-height:14pt; font-family:Times New 
Roman; font-size:12pt"><B>SUBMISSION OF MATTERS TO A VOTE OF SECURITY 
HOLDERS.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March 9, 2004, we 
solicited votes from selected shareholders of record to approve an increase in 
our authorized share capital from 50,000,000 to 150,000,000, par value $0.001 
per share. &nbsp;We received an affirmative vote of 20,354,379 or 51% of our 
issued and outstanding shares (39,944,744 shares).</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December 3, 2004 at our 
Annual General Meeting of Shareholders, shareholders voted in favor of 
increasing the number of options authorized for issuance under the 
Corporation&#146;s 2000 Stock Award Plan from 8,000,000 to 15,000,000. The 
Shareholders also approved a name change from China Energy Ventures Corp. to Big
Sky Energy Corporation. The Shareholders also voted in favor of amending the By-
laws of the Corporation to require a minimum number of board members to be three
and a maximum number to be eleven.</P>

<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>RECENT SALES OF 
UNREGISTERED SECURITIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; text-indent:36pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During 2004, we granted 
100,000 options exercisable to acquire common shares to a consultant. 
&nbsp;These options were priced above the fair market value on the date of grant
with an exercise price of $0.56 per share. The options were subject to vesting 
conditions based upon continued performance of services, pursuant to which one-
third of the granted options vested on the date of grant, and one-third of the 
granted options would prospectively vest on each of the first and second 
anniversaries of the date of grant, respectively.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On January 26, 2004, we 
issued 100,000 shares to an accredited investor at $0.25 per share for gross 
proceeds of $25,000. &nbsp;These securities were issued to a non-U.S. person 
outside the United States.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On February 11, 2004, we 
issued 66,666 shares upon a Stock Option Award being exercised at a price of 
$0.05 per share for gross proceeds of $3,333.30. &nbsp;These securities were 
issued to a non-U.S. person outside the United States.</P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March 4, 2004, the 
Corporation issued 681,475 common shares to Ibriz in connection with an Asset 
Purchase Agreement that we entered into with Ibriz. &nbsp;The amount of common 
stock issued was determined using the average closing price of our common stock 
for the five days prior to February 27, 2004, which resulted in a share price of
$0.61 per share. &nbsp;These securities were issued to a non-U.S. entity outside
the United States.</P>

<BR>
